Question:
In which part of the United Kingdom do traffic officers operate?

A. England and Wales
B. England, Wales and Northern Ireland
C. England only
D. England, Scotland and Wales

Answer: A
Description: Traffic officers have powers to stop vehicles on safety grounds; for example, if you have an insecure load. They only operate in England and Wales. It's an offence not to comply with their directions.
Category: Road and traffic signs

Question:
What's the purpose of an emergency refuge area on a smart motorway?

A. It's for construction and road workers to store emergency equipment 
B. It's for a police patrol to park and watch traffic
C. It's for use if you think you'll be involved in a road-rage incident 
D. It's for use in case of emergency or breakdown

Answer: D
Description: Emergency refuge areas may be found next to the hard shoulder on a smart motorway. If possible, you should use one of these areas, rather than the hard shoulder, when you break down. If the hard shoulder is being used as a running lane, take care when you rejoin the motorway.
Category: Road and traffic signs

Question:
What are traffic officers authorised to do?

A. Carry out enforcement duties
B. Issue fixed penalty notices
C. Test drivers suspected of drink-driving
D. Stop and direct anyone on a motorway

Answer: D
Description: Traffic officers don't have enforcement powers, but they're able to stop and direct people on motorways and some 'A' class roads. They operate in England and Wales and work in partnership with the police at incidents. Traffic officers can be recognised by their orange-and-yellow jackets and their vehicles, which have yellow-and-black markings.

Question:

image: lttk2119.jpg

D. You shouldn't use this lane as a running lane

Answer: D
Description: On smart motorways, the hard shoulder can be used as a running lane when a speed limit is shown above it. However, a red cross above the hard shoulder means that this lane shouldn't be used, except for emergencies and breakdowns.

Question:
You're on a smart motorway. What does it mean when a mandatory speed limit is displayed above the hard shoulder?
image: lttk2120.jpg

A. The hard shoulder can be used as a running lane
B. Large vehicles must use the hard shoulder
C. You shouldn't use the hard shoulder as a running lane
D. You can park on the hard shoulder if you feel tired

Answer: A
Description: If a mandatory speed-limit sign is shown above the hard shoulder, this lane can be used as a running lane. You must stay within the signed speed limit. Look out for any vehicles that have broken down and are blocking the hard shoulder.
Category: Road and traffic signs

Question:
What's the aim of a smart motorway?

A. To prevent tailgating
B. To reduce congestion
C. To prevent overtaking
D. To reduce rest stops

Answer: B
Description: Smart motorways are intended to reduce congestion and make journey times more reliable. In these areas, the hard shoulder may be used as a running lane to ease congestion at peak times or when an incident occurs. The variable speed limits shown in red circles are mandatory and help to keep traffic flowing at a steady speed.
Category: Road and traffic signs

Question:
You're on a smart motorway. What do the speed-limit signs indicate?

A. The speed limit on the sign must be obeyed
B. The national speed limit will always apply
C. The speed limit is always 30 mph
D. The speed limit on the sign is advisory

Answer: A
Description: When a smart motorway is in operation, you must follow the instructions shown on the gantries above each lane. There may also be instructions above the hard shoulder. The signals displayed are mandatory and may be enforced with camera technology.
Category: Road and traffic signs

Question:
You're travelling on a motorway. A red cross is displayed on the gantry signals above the hard shoulder and mandatory speed limits are shown above all other lanes. What does the red cross mean?
image: lttk2121.jpg

A. The hard shoulder can be used as a normal running lane 
B. The hard shoulder can be used as a rest area if you feel tired
C. The hard shoulder is for emergency or breakdown use only
D. The hard shoulder has a speed limit of 50 mph

Answer: C
Description: A red cross above the hard shoulder means that it's closed as a running lane and should only be used for emergencies or breakdowns. At busy times, the hard shoulder may be used as a running lane; the red cross will then be replaced by a mandatory speed-limit sign.

Question:

A. Maintain your speed and sound your horn
B. Stop across the junction until the traffic clears
C. Go forward if your vehicle will clear the junction
D. Drive slowly across the junction

Answer: C
Description: Look well ahead and plan your approach to all junctions. Even if the traffic lights are green, don’t go forward if queuing traffic will cause you to block the junction. Be aware of the length of your vehicle and how much space it needs to clear the junction.

Answer: D

D. Flash your lights to show your annoyance

Answer: B
Description: Some drivers might emerge from a junction when it's not safe to do so. In this situation, understand that other drivers might make mistakes. Don’t intimidate them by driving aggressively to teach them a lesson.

Question:

A. When you're making deliveries that are less than 50 metres apart
B. When you're less than 50 miles away from your depot
C. When you're towing at less than 50 mph
D. When you're working less than 50 hours in a week

Answer: A
Description: It's compulsory for drivers and passengers to wear seat belts. However, if you're making deliveries that are less than 50 metres apart, you may leave the seat belt undone. It would be impractical to keep fastening and unfastening your seat belt over such short distances.

Question:

A. There are speed cameras ahead
B. The lorry is leaving the motorway
C. The lorry is about to overtake
D. Traffic further ahead may be stopping

Answer: D
Description: When someone ahead of you switches on their hazard warning lights, it means that they've spotted a hazard that you may not be able to see yet. Slow down and be ready to stop if necessary.

Question:
What should you do if you lose your way in heavy traffic?

A. Drive on until you find a safe place to stop
B. Stop at traffic lights and ask pedestrians
C. Shout to other drivers to ask them the way
D. Check a map as you keep moving with the traffic

Answer: A
Description: Driving in heavy traffic needs 100% concentration. If you become lost, find a safe place to stop before checking a map or asking for directions. Don’t risk losing concentration by glancing at a map while driving, even if you're in traffic that keeps stopping. 
Category: The driver

Question:
Where are you most likely to find pedestrians stepping into the road?

A. Wooded areas
B. One-way streets
C. Shopping areas
D. Motorways

Answer: C
Description: In shopping areas, pedestrians frequently want to cross the road. They may be hidden by parked vehicles before stepping out into your path. Keep your speed down and be aware of the risk of pedestrians suddenly walking into the road.
Category: The driver

Question:
What's most likely to cause danger to a group of horse riders?

A. Powerful brake lights
B. The noise of your vehicle
C. Leaving plenty of room
D. Reacting too early

Answer: B
Description: The hiss of air-assisted mechanisms, as well as engine noise, can easily startle horses. Keep the noise to a minimum by gentle use of the brakes and, if necessary, stopping and turning your engine off.
Category: The driver

Question:
What should you do when passing sheep on a road?

A. Drive very slowly
B. Pass quickly and quietly
C. Keep your vehicle moving
D. Sound your horn gently

Answer: A
Description: Animals can be very unpredictable. You should give them as much room as you can, keep your speed and noise to a minimum to avoid panicking them, and always be ready to stop if necessary.
Category: The driver

Question:
When is your nearside mirror most likely to endanger pedestrians?

A. When driving past a car park
B. When driving near a hospital
C. When driving close to the kerb
D. When driving over a speed hump

Answer: C
Description: When you drive too close to the kerb, there's a risk that your nearside mirror could strike the head of a pedestrian. Be aware of this hazard and, if you see pedestrians close to the road, make sure you leave them enough room.
Category: The driver

Question:
What can prevent you from holding a bus or lorry driving licence?

B. Skin problems
C. Dyslexia
D. Heart disorders 

Answer: D
Description: An illness that could affect you while you're driving, such as a heart condition, may make it unsafe for you to drive. You must tell DVLA if you develop any serious illness or disability that's likely to last more than three months and that could affect your driving. Partial blindness and mental disorders can also prevent you from getting a driving licence for large vehicles.

Question:
You're driving along this road. What should you do if the red van cuts in close in front of you?
image: lttk2125.jpg

A. Drop back to leave the correct separation distance
B. Give a long blast on the horn
C. Flash your headlights several times
D. Accelerate to get closer to the red van

Answer: A
Description: There are times when other road users make incorrect or ill-judged decisions. Try to stay calm and don’t retaliate or react aggressively, especially as your vehicle is likely to be larger and more intimidating than the other person's. Always put safety first.

Question:
You're approaching a large puddle near the left-hand kerb. What should you do if pedestrians are close to the water?

A. Wave at the pedestrians to keep back 
B. Ignore the puddle
C. Brake suddenly and sound your horn
D. Try to avoid splashing the pedestrians

Answer: D
Description: The effect of your vehicle driving through a puddle will be to throw water onto the pavement. If there are pedestrians close by, they could be splashed with the water. Be considerate and, if it’s safe to do so, avoid driving through the puddle.
Category: The driver

Question:
What should you do if a long, heavily laden lorry is taking a long time to overtake you?

A. Speed up
B. Change direction
C. Slow down
D. Hold your speed

Answer: C
Description: A long lorry with a heavy load will need more time to pass you than a car. It won’t be able to accelerate enough to pass you quickly, especially on an uphill stretch of road. Be considerate to the lorry driver – ease off the accelerator and allow the lorry to pass.
Category: The driver

Question:
You're driving a slow-moving vehicle on a narrow, winding road. What should you do to let other vehicles overtake you?

A. Wave them past
B. Show a left-turn signal
C. Stop in a safe place
D. Drive more slowly

Answer: C
Description: Don’t frustrate other road users by driving for long distances with a queue of traffic behind you. This could cause them to lose concentration and overtake in an unsafe way. Stop where it's safe and let them pass.
Category: The driver

Question:
When should you use your vehicle's horn?

A. To allow you right of way
B. To warn others of your presence
C. To greet other road users
D. To signal your annoyance

Answer: B
Description: Only use your horn to warn people of your presence when they may not have seen you. Don’t use it to greet others, to show impatience, or to give or claim priority. 
Your horn mustn't be used between 11.30 pm and 7.00 am in a built-up area, or when your vehicle is stationary, unless another vehicle poses a danger.
Category: The driver

Question:
You're following a car being driven slowly by a learner driver. What should you do if it isn't safe to overtake it?

A. Flash your lights so the driver sees you
B. Drive along the centre line of the road
C. Be patient and stay well behind
D. Switch your hazard lights on 

Answer: C
Description: Learner drivers are often nervous. If you stay well back, this will reduce the risk of incidents occurring if they make a mistake, and you won't intimidate them. Remember, you were once in that situation yourself.

Question:

Description: If a police officer signals for you to stop, stop as soon as possible in a safe place on the left.

Question:

C. Signal with the left indicator
D. Switch on the hazard warning lights

Answer: C
Description: When a police officer is following you and wants you to stop, they'll flash the vehicle's headlights and signal with the left indicator. You should stop in a safe place as soon as possible.

Question:
Your vehicle is fitted with a hand-held telephone. What should you do before taking or making a call?

A. Steer your vehicle with one hand
B. Reduce your speed to less than 30 mph
C. Be very careful when dealing with junctions
D. Find a safe place to stop

Answer: D
Description: Telephone calls can distract you, meaning that you're not in proper control of your vehicle. If you need to use a telephone when driving, find a safe place to stop first. Better still, use a phone answering service and listen to your messages at the end of your journey.
Category: The driver

Question:
A mobile telephone is fitted to your vehicle. When should it be used?

A. When travelling slowly
B. When you're stopped in a safe place
C. When in light traffic
D. When on a motorway

Answer: B
Description: It’s illegal to use a hand-held phone while driving. When you've stopped in a safe place, you can concentrate on your call or message. Using a phone while driving means you won’t have full control of your vehicle. This could result in a collision, with serious or even fatal consequences.
Category: The driver

Question:
You approach a pelican crossing that goes straight across the road. How must you treat it if it has a central island?

A. As one crossing in daylight only
B. As two separate crossings
C. As one continuous crossing
D. As two crossings during darkness

Answer: C
Description: A pelican crossing that goes straight across the road must be treated as one continuous crossing even if it has a central island. The lights controlling the crossing show to both directions of traffic. You must give way to pedestrians who are still crossing when the amber light is flashing.
Category: The driver

Question:
What does the flashing amber light mean at a pelican crossing?

A. Stop and wait for the green light
B. Give way to pedestrians already on the crossing
C. Stop if you can do so safely
D. Give way to pedestrians waiting to cross

Answer: B
Description: Pedestrians use push-button controls to activate the signals. Pelican crossings have no red-and-amber stage before green. Instead, they have a flashing amber light. This means you must give way to pedestrians on the crossing, but you may proceed if the crossing is clear.
Category: The driver

Question:
What should you do at a zebra crossing?

A. Always leave the crossing clear in traffic queues
B. Rev your engine to encourage pedestrians to cross quickly
C. Wave pedestrians to cross if you intend to wait for them
D. Park only on the zigzag lines on the left

Answer: A
Description: When traffic is heavy, plan well ahead so that you don’t block crossings. Leave them clear so that pedestrians can cross safely. 
Category: The driver

Question:
A coach is overtaking you. What should you do when it's safe for the coach to move back to the left?

A. Flash your headlights once
B. Switch your sidelights on and off
C. Do nothing and let the driver decide
D. Flash your headlights twice

Answer: C
Description: When you're being overtaken, the other driver has to decide when it's safe to complete the manoeuvre. Don't give an unofficial signal, however well intended. There may be a hazard you're unable to see from your position.
Category: The driver

Question:

D. Ignore it if possible, unless you're forced to let it pass

Answer: C
Description: When an ambulance is displaying a flashing blue light, try to stop in a safe place to allow it to pass. Make sure you don't endanger any other road users or commit an offence; for example, by driving past a red traffic light.

Question:
Should you give way to a car showing a flashing green beacon?

A. Yes, because it's a doctor going to an emergency
B. Yes, because it's a fire-crew support vehicle
C. No, because it's a breakdown vehicle
D. No, because it's a slow-moving vehicle

Answer: A
Description: If you see a vehicle with a green flashing light, it will be a doctor on an emergency call, so give way by pulling over and letting the vehicle pass. But don't just stop suddenly – choose a safe place as soon as you can to let the doctor’s car pass safely.
Category: The driver

Question:
What type of emergency vehicle has a green flashing beacon?

A. Fire engine
B. Doctor’s car
C. Ambulance
D. Road gritter

Answer: B
Description: A green flashing light on a vehicle means the driver or passenger is a doctor on an emergency call. Give way to them if it’s safe to do so. Be aware that the vehicle may be travelling quickly or may stop suddenly.
Category: The driver

Question:
You stop for pedestrians at a zebra crossing. What should you do if they don't start to cross immediately?

A. Drive on
B. Be patient and wait
C. Wave them to cross
D. Sound your horn

Answer: B
Description: If you stop for pedestrians and they don’t start to cross, be patient. Don’t wave them across or sound your horn. This could be dangerous if the driver of an approaching vehicle isn't aware of them. The driver may not have seen or heard your signal, making it very dangerous for the pedestrians to start to cross.
Category: The driver

Question:
Why could it be dangerous to wave people across at pedestrian crossings?

A. They may not see your signal
B. There may be another vehicle coming
C. They may be distracted
D. They may not be ready to cross

Answer: B
Description: You should always try to stop, if it's safe, for people waiting at pedestrian crossings. However, avoid waving them to cross. Another driver may not have seen them, may not have seen your signal or may not be able to stop safely.
Category: The driver

Question:

• Pedestrians may step off the kerb. 
• The nearside mirror may be at a pedestrian’s head height. 
• Cyclists may be tempted to pass you on your left if you're driving slowly in congested conditions.

Question:

What should you do if a vehicle comes up quickly behind, flashing its headlights?

A. Touch the brake pedal sharply to show your brake lights
B. Maintain your speed and prevent the vehicle from overtaking
C. Accelerate to maintain a gap behind you
D. Allow the vehicle to overtake

Answer: D
Description: Don’t try to enforce the speed limit by blocking another vehicle’s progress. This is likely to cause the other driver to become more frustrated. Slow down or move over when it's safe and allow the other vehicle to pass.

Question:
What should you do when a vehicle pulls out in front of you at a junction?

A. Flash your headlights and drive up close behind
B. Swerve past it and sound your horn
C. Accelerate past it immediately
D. Slow down and be ready to stop

Answer: D
Description: Plan ahead and learn to anticipate hazards. Give yourself more time to react to any problems that might occur – such as a vehicle pulling out unexpectedly. Be tolerant of other road users who don’t behave correctly. Don't react by flashing your lights, sounding your horn or making gestures, as any show of aggression on the road can quickly lead to a serious incident.
Category: The driver

Question:
How is drinking alcohol likely to affect your driving?

A. You'll become colour-blind
B. You'll be able to concentrate better
C. You'll feel more confident
D. You'll have faster reactions

Answer: C
Description: Alcohol can increase confidence to a point where a driver’s behaviour might become ‘out of character’: someone who normally behaves sensibly suddenly takes risks and enjoys it. Never let yourself or your friends get into this situation.

Question:
What can seriously affect your concentration while driving?

A. Tinted windows
B. Fresh air
C. Contact lenses
D. Tiredness

Answer: D
Description: Tiredness can seriously affect your concentration – even to the point of falling asleep. You always need to be alert so that you can safely deal with the constantly changing environment around your vehicle.
Category: The driver

Question:
How does alcohol affect your driving?

A. It increases your awareness
B. It improves your coordination
C. It reduces your concentration
D. It speeds up your reactions

Answer: C
Description: Concentration and good judgement are needed to be a good, safe driver. You're strongly advised not to drink any alcohol before driving. Alcohol can stay in your system for 24–48 hours, so you should also consider your intake the day and night before driving.
Category: The driver

Question:

C. Insurance premiums
D. Vehicle test certificate

Answer: C
Description: If you've been convicted of drink- or drug-driving, statistically you're a risk to yourself and others on the road. For this reason, when you're able to drive again, insurance companies may charge you a high premium to insure your vehicle.

Question:
What should you do if you've had a few alcoholic drinks at a party?

B. Have a strong cup of coffee and then drive home
C. Go home by public transport
D. Wait a short while and then drive home

Answer: C
Description: Drinking black coffee or waiting a few hours won’t make any difference. Alcohol takes time to leave the body, so you should find a way to get home without using your vehicle; for example, by public transport. Depending on how much you've had to drink, you may even be unfit to drive the following morning.
Category: The driver

B. Avoid drinking alcohol completely
C. Drink plenty of coffee after drinking alcohol
D. Avoid drinking alcohol on an empty stomach

Answer: B
Description: Avoiding alcohol will always be the safest option. There are many factors that influence how alcohol will affect you, such as height, weight and gender. It's better not to risk a single alcoholic drink before you drive.

Question:

• be decisive at intersections and junctions
• plan your rest stops
• know approximately how long the journey will take.

Question:

Question:
What should you do if a front tyre bursts while you're driving on a motorway?

B. Loosen your grip on the steering wheel
C. Drive to the next service area
D. Hold the steering wheel firmly

Answer: D
Description: A front tyre bursting will seriously reduce your control of the vehicle. Keep calm and resist the temptation to brake hard or swerve. Hold the steering wheel firmly and try to get the vehicle onto the hard shoulder while allowing it to slow down gradually. Stop as far to the left as possible and switch on your hazard warning lights.

Question:

B. When you switch on the heated rear window
C. When you switch on the windscreen wipers
D. When you look at the door mirrors

Answer: A
Description: Using a hand-held mobile phone while driving is illegal. It will distract you from your driving, because your attention is split between the phone call and your driving.

Question:

Answer: C

Switch it off before you start driving and use the messaging facility. You can pick up messages when you stop for a rest break. If you must make a call, stop in a safe place before using the phone.

Question:

Question:

Answer: D

Question:

C. It prevents you from oversteering
D. It only works at high speeds

Answer: B
Description: Power-assisted steering operates when the engine is running. If a fault develops, much greater effort is required to turn the steering wheel. Don't attempt to drive a vehicle if you're aware of a fault in the power-steering system.

B. Flash your headlights several times

Answer: A
Description: Sometimes other drivers or riders make a mistake. If this happens, try not to let it worry you. Question:

C. Move forward and wait in the middle
D. Edge out slowly so other traffic will see you

Answer: A
Description: When turning right onto a dual carriageway, don’t stop in the gap in the central reservation unless your vehicle will fit in the gap without any overhang. When it’s busy, consider turning left and using a roundabout further up the road so you don't have to cross the central reservation.

Question:

D. The camber of the road

Answer: C
Description: Plan well ahead and take care if you need to move out or straddle lanes due to the length of your vehicle. It’s better to use extra space on the road you’re leaving than to find there's not enough room when you turn in.

Question:
What should you do when you have to travel a long distance?

B. Allow plenty of time for your journey
C. Avoid all national-speed-limit roads
D. Plan to go at busy times

Answer: B
Description: Always allow plenty of time for your journey, in case of unforeseen problems such as punctures, breakdowns, road closures or diversions. You'll feel less stressed and less inclined to take risks if you're not under time pressure.

Question:
What can you do to help maintain concentration while you're driving?

A. Don't eat at all when on duty
B. Have regular meals and rest breaks
C. Eat sugary snacks when on duty
D. Avoid meals containing bread

Answer: B
Description: Being as healthy and alert as possible will make you safer on the road. Take regular meal and rest breaks, and keep to foods that contain complex carbohydrates, such as bread and vegetables. These release energy slowly and will keep you satisfied for longer than foods with a high sugar content.
Category: The driver

Question:
What's the best type of fluid to drink during work time?

A. Sugary canned drinks
B. Hot chocolate
C. High-caffeine drinks
D. Bottled water

Answer: D
Description: Water is the ideal drink, because it quenches your thirst for longer than tea or coffee. It's a good idea to carry water when you're driving, especially in very hot weather. The medical profession recommends that you drink 1.5 to 2 litres of water per day. 
Category: The driver

Question:
What should you do to help your concentration when you have to drive through the night?

A. Eat a meal at the beginning of your shift
B. Eat lots of snacks while you're driving 
C. Eat a big meal in the middle of your shift
D. Eat nothing during your period of work

Answer: A
Description: Concentration will be improved by eating regular, light meals timed to fit in with your scheduled rest periods. If you don't eat at all, your blood sugar levels will drop and you'll feel tired. If you just eat snack foods, most of which are sugary or high in fat, your energy levels will peak and then drop – and eating while you're driving is a dangerous distraction.
Category: The driver

Question:
When is there a particular risk of sleep-related incidents?

A. Between 2 am and 7 am
B. Between 11 pm and 2 am
C. Between 6 pm and 11 pm
D. Between 7 am and 2 pm

Answer: A
Description: There's a particular risk when driving between 2 am and 7 am. This is when the ’body clock’ is programmed for sleep in most people. There's another, smaller, dip between 2 pm and 4 pm. If you feel that tiredness is affecting your ability to drive, stop in a safe place and rest.
Category: The driver

Question:

A. 40%
B. 70%
C. 95%
D. 55%

Answer: A
Description: Research shows that approximately 40% of SRVIs involve commercial vehicles. The consequences are usually very serious because of the size of the vehicle and the fact that there is no braking before the impact.
Category: The driver

Question:

A. Epilepsy
B. Heart disease
C. Lung disease
D. Deafness

Answer: B
Description: A poor diet can increase your risk of ill health. It may cause obesity, diabetes or heart disease, which can increase your risk of sudden incapacity at the wheel. There's a greater risk of developing a serious illness – and ultimately an early death. Smoking and a lack of exercise will increase the risks.
Category: The driver

Question:
What should you do when you've been driving for a long time and are fighting sleep?

A. Stop and rest
B. Stretch your arms 
C. Play loud music 
D. Open a window

Answer: A
Description: The only effective solution to driver sleepiness is to stop in a safe place and take a break. 
Category: The driver

Question:
Where do most sleep-related vehicle incidents occur?

A. On motorways
B. On tourist routes
C. In one-way streets
D. On rural roads

Answer: A
Description: Driving at a constant speed for long periods, such as on a motorway, can cause drowsiness. Falling asleep while driving accounts for a significant proportion of vehicle incidents. You should plan and take regular rest stops, but if you feel the onset of tiredness between these breaks, stop and rest in a safe place. 
Category: The driver

Question:
At what age are men most at risk from sleep-related vehicle incidents (SRVIs)?

A. 31–45 years
B. 46–59 years
C. 60 years and over
D. 30 years and under

Answer: D
Description: SRVIs are more evident in young male drivers, who tend to ignore or deny how they're feeling. The greatest risk is between the hours of 2.00 am and 7.00 am, when the body clock is in a trough. Make sure you take sufficient rest breaks and don't ignore feeling sleepy.
Category: The driver

Question:
What should you try to do when your vehicle has a front-tyre blow-out?

A. Brake hard and steer towards the affected side
B. Hold the steering wheel firmly and slow down gradually
C. Steer to the right-hand side and brake firmly
D. Don't use your brakes under any circumstances

Answer: B
Description: With a front-tyre blow-out, you won't be able to steer properly. Keep a firm hold of the steering wheel and slow gradually to a stop. Don’t brake hard or steer sharply.
Category: The driver

Question:
When can you drive without wearing a seat belt?

A. When the speed limit is 30 mph or less
B. When you hold a medical exemption certificate
C. When the seat belt is too large for your use
D. When you're driving on a motorway

Answer: B
Description: When seat belts are fitted to your vehicle, they must be worn unless you hold a valid medical exemption certificate. People making deliveries or collections in goods vehicles are also exempt, when they're travelling less than 50 metres (162 feet).
Category: The driver

Question:
How will your body clock affect your driving between 2.00 am and 7.00 am?

A. You're more likely to break the speed limit
B. You're more likely to drive too close to the vehicle in front
C. You're more likely to feel road rage
D. You're more likely to fall asleep at the wheel

Answer: D
Description: A significant number of sleep-related vehicle incidents involve commercial vehicles. There's a particular risk when driving between 2.00 am and 7.00 am, because this is when the body clock craves sleep. It’s important to take proper rest before, during and between driving duties. 
Category: The driver

Question:
What's provided specifically to protect you against neck and whiplash injuries?

A. A head restraint
B. An air-sprung seat
C. A collapsible steering wheel
D. Anti-lock brakes

Answer: A
Description: If you’re in a collision, a properly adjusted head restraint can help to reduce the risk of neck injury. However, an incorrectly adjusted head restraint could worsen any damage to your neck. 
Category: The driver

Question:
What should you do when you overtake a cyclist on a two-way road? 

A. Leave plenty of room and check your nearside mirror before returning to the left
B. Give a right-turn signal after you've moved out to overtake
C. Go past quickly and move back to the left sharply
D. Pass closely, staying about 1 metre (3 feet 3 inches) from the kerb

Answer: A
Description: Only overtake when it's safe to do so, and don't use the size of your vehicle to intimidate approaching traffic. When overtaking a cyclist, leave plenty of room and, before returning to the left, check in your nearside mirror to make sure you've passed them safely. 
Category: The road

Question:
Your lorry has a curtain-sided body. Your route will take you over several high-level bridges. Why should you check the weather forecast before starting your journey? 

A. In hot weather, the bridges might be closed to heavy traffic
B. High-level bridges may be closed to certain vehicles in windy weather
C. Rain can make crossing bridges very difficult for large vehicles
D. You won’t be able to cross the bridges if it’s frosty

Answer: B
Description: In exposed places, such as high-level bridges, viaducts or some motorways, high winds can cause the road to be closed to certain vehicles. If you’re driving a high-sided vehicle and high winds are forecast, plan an alternative route in case your intended route is closed.
Category: The road

Question:
What should you do when you want to join a motorway where traffic is flowing freely?

A. Stop at the start of the slip road and move off when you see a gap
B. Build up your speed on the slip road before joining the motorway
C. Keep to a low speed until you see a gap on the motorway
D. Use the hard shoulder, if necessary, to build up speed

Answer: B
Description: Normally, you should avoid having to stop before joining a motorway. Use the slip road to build up your speed so that you can emerge safely. If it’s extremely busy, there may be rare occasions when you have to stop and then filter into the traffic. This is most likely to happen where traffic is queuing; for example, at roadworks. 
Category: The road

Question:

A. Check your spray-suppression equipment
B. Check your wind deflector
C. Plan your route in advance
D. Only half-load your lorry

Answer: C
Description: In high winds, some exposed roads, bridges and viaducts are closed to high-sided vehicles. Plan your route with care and try to avoid these areas. Also plan an alternative route in case of road closure.
Category: The road

Question:
You're overtaking another lorry. What should you do if you start to lose speed due to an uphill gradient?

A. Try to force the vehicle you were overtaking to speed up
B. Continue at the same speed and in the same position
C. Ease off and drop behind the vehicle you were trying to overtake
D. Try to force the vehicle you were overtaking to drop back

Answer: C
Description: If you try to overtake another vehicle and realise that you’re unable to complete the manoeuvre, ease off the accelerator and drop back behind the vehicle. If the vehicle you’re trying to overtake is large, then it will take a long time to pass. You should assess whether you have the time and power to complete the manoeuvre before you try to overtake.
Category: The road

Question:
How could you reduce the problems caused by a strong side wind when driving an empty curtain-sided vehicle on an exposed bridge?

A. Tie open the curtain on the side the wind's blowing from
B. Tie both curtains open
C. Tie one curtain open and lock open the rear doors
D. Leave both curtains closed

Answer: B
Description: If you’re driving an empty curtain-sided vehicle, you can help to lower the resistance to side wind if you tie the curtains open. The air will then be able to flow across the flat bed of the vehicle. This will reduce any loss of control, particularly when crossing exposed viaducts or bridges.
Category: The road

Question:
When is a high-sided vehicle most affected by side wind?

A. When it's stationary
B. When it's travelling empty
C. When it's being reversed
D. When it's travelling loaded

Answer: B
Description: Take care if you're driving an empty high-sided vehicle when it’s windy. Watch for places where the conditions could suddenly change, such as a gap between buildings or when passing under a bridge. Reduce your speed and stay alert for other road users who are also affected by these weather conditions.
Category: The road

Question:
You're driving an empty curtain-sided vehicle. Why might you consider tying the curtains open?

A. It's a legal requirement
B. To reduce the effect of side wind
C. To use less fuel
D. To prevent the curtains from tearing

Answer: B
Description: Closed curtains on large empty vehicles can hold the wind. Strong side wind can blow a semi-trailer off course and, in severe cases, can blow the whole vehicle over onto its side. To reduce the risk of this happening, you should tie the curtains open.

Question:
Which of these vehicles is most at risk from strong side wind?

A. An unladen lorry with platform body
B. An unladen lorry with box body
C. A laden lorry with box body
D. A laden lorry with platform body

Answer: B
Description: An unladen vehicle that also has high sides will be vulnerable to the effects of strong side wind. An evenly distributed load will help to keep the vehicle more stable, but the higher the vehicle is, the more it will be affected. Be aware that such a vehicle may become unstable or difficult to control in windy conditions.

B. A car

Question:
Which vehicle is most at risk in windy conditions?

A. High-sided lorry
B. Saloon car
C. Single-deck bus
D. Tractor unit

Answer: A
Description: High-sided vehicles are severely affected by side wind because of the large surface area of the bodywork. The risk of loss of control is increased if the vehicle is unladen.

Question:
When are air deflectors most effective?

A. When there's a strong tailwind
B. When there's a headwind
C. When reversing
D. When there's a side wind

Answer: B
Description: Air deflectors reduce wind resistance by streamlining the vehicle. They're most effective when there's a headwind. The streamlining also reduces the vehicle's fuel consumption.

Question:
What ground conditions are suitable for a tipper lorry to tip its load?

A. Soft and downhill
B. Solid and level
C. Solid and uphill
D. Soft and level

Answer: B
Description: When discharging a load from a tipper vehicle, the centre of gravity is raised as the tipper body rises. To avoid the vehicle rolling over, it’s vital that it's positioned on a level, solid surface before the tipper mechanism is engaged.

Question:
What might happen if using the brakes continuously causes them to overheat?

A. The brake pedal will become stiff
B. The brakes will work better
C. The air pressure will increase
D. The brakes will be less effective

Answer: D
Description: Whenever you brake, the brakes convert the moving energy of your vehicle into heat. Continuous use of the brakes, particularly from high speed or on long steep descents, can cause the shoes and drums to overheat. This will make them less effective and, in some cases, they may not work at all.

Question:

Answer: A
Description: When you’re in a warm cab, you may not notice the drop in outside temperature. One of the first signs of an icy road is a lack of ‘feel’ in the steering. If this happens, slow down and increase the distance between your vehicle and the one in front.

Question:

Answer: A

Question:

A. Ease off the accelerator
B. Brake very sharply 
C. Increase your speed
D. Steer towards the centre line

Answer: A
Description: In wet conditions, water can build up between your tyres and the road surface. This is known as aquaplaning and it will cause your vehicle to slide. Try to regain control by easing off the accelerator to gradually lose speed. Don't brake or steer until your tyres are gripping the road again.

Question:

Answer: A
Description: A buffer lane is used when the wind begins to cause a risk to high-sided vehicles. At other times, it will be a normal lane. Don’t use the buffer lane unless your vehicle has been blown off course into the lane, or you need to use it to avoid an incident or collision.

Question:

Question:

D. A loaded tanker

Question:

Question:

Question:

Description: You must check the nearside mirror during and after overtaking a motorcyclist. Make sure that the rider is still in control and that your vehicle's draught hasn't caused them to lose their balance.

Question:

Question:

Answer: A

Question:

A. To avoid puncturing the tyres
B. To avoid splashing pedestrians
C. To improve their view around the bend
D. To reduce the risk of skidding

Answer: D
Description: Drain covers usually have a metal surface. When wet, these covers are slippery and can cause a motorcycle to skid; be prepared for riders to avoid them.

Question:
What's the minimum distance you should allow for braking when it's raining heavily?

A. Five times the normal distance
B. The normal distance
C. Three times the normal distance
D. Twice the normal distance

Answer: D
Description: If you’re travelling in heavy rain, you should be aware that it could take twice as long for you to stop as it would in dry weather. Increase your distance from the vehicle in front to allow for the longer stopping distance.
Category: The road

Question:
You're driving on a motorway. What should you do if your view ahead is restricted by heavy spray?

A. Leave the motorway at the next exit
B. Use the two-second rule
C. Move into the lane on the right
D. Switch on your dipped headlights

Answer: D
Description: If you’re travelling on a motorway and your view ahead is poor, then you should reduce your speed. Leave at least four seconds between your vehicle and the one in front, and make sure that others can see you by using your dipped headlights.
Category: The road

Question:
What's the greatest risk to your safety when you're overtaking on a motorway in very wet weather?

A. Your braking distance may be reduced
B. Your engine may get flooded
C. Your steering may become heavy
D. Your tyres may lose grip

Answer: D
Description: In very wet conditions, tyres may be unable to clear all the water from their path. This can result in a layer of water building up between the road and the tyre – a situation known as aquaplaning. To regain control, ease off the accelerator and, as the vehicle slows, the tyres should regain their grip. It's safer to reduce the risk of aquaplaning occurring by driving more slowly in very wet weather.
Category: The road

Question:
What should you be aware of when you're overtaking on a motorway while it's raining heavily?

A. Manhole covers will be slippery
B. Visibility will be reduced by spray from traffic
C. There'll be distracting bright reflections
D. Your braking distances will be reduced

Answer: B
Description: Other road users can be affected by the spray from large vehicles, severely reducing their vision. Always take care when you need to change lanes: signal in good time and watch your mirrors carefully before pulling out in these conditions.
Category: The road

Question:
Why can visibility be worse when driving at high speed in wet weather?

A. Headlights will dazzle you more easily
B. More spray will be thrown up
C. Windscreen wipers obstruct your view
D. Drivers bunch together when it's raining

Answer: B
Description: Higher speeds will cause more spray to be thrown up by vehicles' tyres – particularly the tyres of larger vehicles and trailers. Always use dipped headlights in poor visibility caused by rain and spray.
Category: The road

Question:
What should you do if you intend to overtake a lorry that's throwing up spray?

A. Move out earlier than normal
B. Get much closer before moving out
C. Wait until the other driver gives a left signal
D. Wait for the lorry to slow down on a hill

Answer: A
Description: If you wish to overtake a vehicle that’s throwing up spray, move out earlier than normal. This will help to limit the reduction in vision that the rear spray will cause before you pass.
Category: The road

Question:
You're driving in wet weather. What effect will faulty spray-suppression equipment have on other drivers?

A. Their vision will be increased
B. They'll need to use intermittent wipers
C. They'll be able to overtake more easily
D. Their vision will be reduced

Answer: D
Description: Spray-suppression equipment reduces the amount of spray thrown up to other road users. Check the equipment regularly to make sure it's secure and undamaged. 
Category: The road

Question:
Why are brushes fitted to this vehicle's wheel arch?
image: lttk2132.jpg

A. To clear mud from the tyres on building sites
B. To stop snow building up behind the wheel
C. To reduce spray on wet roads
D. To remove objects from the tyre tread

Answer: C
Description: The brushes are part of a spray-suppression system. They reduce the amount of water thrown up at the sides and rear of the vehicle. Check them regularly for security. If they become worn, make sure they're replaced.

Question:
When should you check your vehicle’s spray-suppression equipment?

A. Only as part of a pre-winter check
B. Before setting out on every journey
C. Once per year before the MOT test
D. Only when you'll be using a motorway

Answer: B
Description: You should always check all your spray-suppression equipment before a journey. Don't ignore it just because it's dry when you set out. The weather can change on the way.
Category: The road

Question:
What component fitted to your vehicle will help following drivers in wet weather?

A. Catalytic converter
B. Wind deflectors
C. Spray reducers
D. Side-panel skirts

Answer: C
Description: Spray reducers or spray-suppression equipment are attachments fitted around the wheel arches of large vehicles. They effectively trap spray thrown up from the wheels, which would otherwise reduce visibility for other road users. 
Category: The road

Question:
This vehicle is fitted with spray-suppression equipment. In what weather conditions will it be most useful?
image: lttk2132.jpg

A. Fog
B. Snow
C. Rain
D. Wind

Answer: C
Description: The spray-suppression equipment helps to prevent water from being thrown up and causing reduced visibility, for you and other drivers. Driving at a reduced speed in wet conditions will also help to reduce the amount of water thrown up by your vehicle's tyres.
Category: The road

Question:
How should you drive through flood water?

A. Slowly, in a high gear, with engine speed low
B. At normal speed when you have spray reducers fitted
C. Slowly, in a low gear, with engine speed high
D. As quickly as possible to cause the least delay

Answer: C
Description: It's important to use a low gear and keep the engine speed high to prevent water from entering the engine through the exhaust system. In these circumstances, it may be necessary to slip the clutch to keep the road speed as low as possible.
Category: The road

Question:
You're on a motorway, approaching a working snow plough. Why should you stay behind it?

A. Your speed could cause snow to drift behind
B. There may be deep snow ahead
C. It's illegal to overtake snow ploughs
D. Snow ploughs are left-hand-drive only

Answer: B
Description: There's no way of knowing how deep the snow could be ahead. If you overtake and then become stuck in the snow, you may cause problems for the snow plough, particularly if you block the road.
Category: The road

Question:
You're driving in heavy rain. Why do you need to increase your distance from the vehicle in front?

A. To reduce the risk of water spraying into the filters
B. To let other motorists move into the gap
C. To allow for an increased stopping distance
D. To prevent rain from entering the vehicle’s braking system

Answer: C
Description: Extra care is needed when driving in heavy rain. Reduce your speed and switch on dipped headlights. Tyres will have less grip on a wet road and it will take up to twice the distance to stop when compared with good dry conditions.
Category: The road

Question:
You're driving a large vehicle in heavy rain on a motorway. You slow down to reduce the risk of aquaplaning. For what other reason should you slow down? 

A. To stop the electrics getting wet
B. To force other drivers to act properly and slow down
C. To prevent water from entering the braking system
D. To reduce the amount of spray thrown up

Answer: D
Description: Driving at high speed on a wet motorway can throw up dense spray, making it very difficult for other drivers to see ahead. Driving more slowly reduces the amount of spray and this makes it safer for other drivers.
Category: The road

Question:
You're driving on a motorway in heavy rain. When are you allowed to use high-intensity rear fog lights?

B. Only when the national speed limit applies
C. When visibility is reduced to 100 metres (328 feet) or less
D. When visibility is more than 100 metres (328 feet) 

Answer: C
Description: Heavy rain and the resulting spray from large vehicles travelling at speed can seriously affect visibility on the motorway. Reduce your speed and use your headlights. Don't use high-intensity rear lights unless visibility is reduced to 100 metres (328 feet) or less.
Category: The road

Question:

Answer: B
Description: If a build-up of water prevents the tyres from gripping the road, the steering can become unresponsive. If this happens, ease off the accelerator and slow down gradually.

C. It will need more engine power
D. It will take longer to stop

Answer: D
Description: When driving downhill, gravity will cause the vehicle to increase speed. More braking effort will be required, and stopping distances will increase.

Description: You must be able to stop safely in the distance that you can see to be clear ahead. This will be the distance illuminated by your headlights or by street lights and will generally be less than you can see in daylight.

Question:

C. The right-hand lane

Answer: B
Description: The red studs on your left indicate the edge of the hard shoulder, while the white studs are used between the lanes. Using more than one reference point will help you to be certain of your position.

Question:

Question:

A. The right-hand lane
B. The middle lane

Answer: D
Description: You should remain in the left-hand lane unless you're overtaking other vehicles. Don’t be inconsiderate and stay in the centre lane or other overtaking lanes when you've finished overtaking.

Question:

C. Move to the next lane if it's safe
D. Expect them to stop and let you pass

Answer: C
Description: Only change lanes if doing so won't inconvenience another road user. Merging drivers have a responsibility to give way, if necessary, and not force their way onto the main carriageway. Planning ahead will ensure you're prepared to deal with these situations.

Question:

Description: Always indicate your intentions in good time; this will allow others time to alter their speed and course if necessary. Always check your blind spots before changing lanes.

Question:
When may vehicles over 7.5 tonnes maximum authorised mass (MAM) use the right-hand lane of a motorway to overtake?

B. When the motorway has three lanes

D. When vehicles are stopped on the hard shoulder

Answer: A
Description: Goods and passenger vehicles with a MAM of more than 7.5 tonnes, those required to be fitted with a speed limiter, and vehicles towing trailers must not use the right-hand lane on a motorway with more than two lanes, unless there are exceptional circumstances. 
Category: The road

Question:

A. Changing gear
B. Increasing your speed
C. Cutting in
D. Signalling

Answer: C
Description: After overtaking, check your nearside mirror carefully before moving back to the left. Don’t rely on the other driver flashing their headlights, because only you can make the decision that it's safe.
Category: The road

Question:
What's a crawler lane for?

A. To enable emergency vehicles to get quickly to the scene of an incident 
B. To enable other traffic to overtake on the nearside
C. To enable slow-moving traffic to move further over to the left on uphill gradients
D. To enable large vehicles to park out of the way

Answer: C
Description: On a motorway where there’s a long uphill gradient, there may be a crawler lane. This helps the traffic to flow by making an extra lane available on the left for slower, heavy vehicles.
Category: The road

Question:
What does this motorway sign mean?
image: lttk2126.jpg

A. You're approaching a service area
B. You're approaching a long downhill slope
C. You're approaching a long uphill slope
D. You're approaching a ‘lorries only’ lane

Answer: C
Description: The term ‘crawler lane’ doesn’t mean the lane is only for extremely slow vehicles. It's advising you of an extra lane on the left. Crawler lanes are usually built on sections of road where the length of the gradient is such that some large vehicles will be slowed to the point where they become a hazard for other road users.
Category: The road

Question:
When should you use a crawler lane?

A. When letting faster traffic overtake you
B. When turning right from a major road
C. When parking to have a rest
D. When slowing down for a motorway exit

Answer: A
Description: Many vehicles are very powerful and can maintain speed even when climbing a gradient. Even if your vehicle is capable of maintaining speed, you can still use the crawler lane to make it easier for other road users to overtake safely.
Category: The road

Question:
What should you do before overtaking on a single carriageway road?

A. Make a final check in your left-hand mirror
B. Flash your headlights at oncoming traffic
C. Look ahead for road junctions
D. Drive very close to the vehicle in front

Answer: C
Description: Before overtaking, you need to make sure it's safe to carry out the manoeuvre. As part of your check, look well ahead for road junctions. You shouldn't overtake as you approach a road junction, because if a vehicle emerges, or has to wait to turn, you could risk a collision.
Category: The road

Question:
When shouldn't you overtake?

A. When your view of the road ahead is clear
B. When the speed limit has been reduced
C. When you're approaching motorway slip roads
D. When you would have to break the speed limit

Answer: D
Description: Never commit yourself to overtaking unless you're absolutely certain that you have the time and space to complete the manoeuvre safely. Don’t take any risks that will endanger other road users.
Category: The road

Question:
You've just overtaken another large vehicle. How do you know when it's safe to move back to the nearside lane?

A. By waiting for the driver you've overtaken to flash their headlights
B. By checking your nearside mirror
C. By moving to the nearside, hoping the other vehicle will slow down
D. By using your hazard warning lights as a signal

Answer: B
Description: While overtaking, you’ll need to judge carefully when to return to the nearside lane. Check your left-hand (nearside) mirror to make sure the rear of your vehicle is well clear. You should allow for the length of both vehicles and take into account the speed difference. Don’t cut in too soon on the vehicle you’ve overtaken, and don’t rely on signals from other drivers; they may be signalling to someone else.
Category: The road

Question:
You're driving on a dual carriageway and intend to overtake the vehicle ahead. What should you do if there's a car approaching quickly behind you in the right-hand lane?

A. Move up closer to the slower vehicle
B. Signal left while waiting for the car to pass
C. Stay behind the slower vehicle
D. Signal right and move out

Answer: C
Description: You should allow the faster-moving vehicle to overtake safely. If you pull out to overtake at this time, you'll cause the car behind to brake sharply. Don’t use the size of your vehicle to intimidate. Be professional and show consideration to other road users. 
Category: The road

Question:
What should you do after overtaking on a dual carriageway?

A. Indicate left, then right
B. Switch your rear lights on and off
C. Move back to the left when it's safe to do so
D. Wait for the other driver to flash their headlights

Answer: C
Description: Signal if necessary and move back to the left as soon as it's safe to do so. Don’t drive for long distances in the centre or right-hand lane unnecessarily.
Category: The road

Question:
You're driving a long vehicle and want to turn right at a roundabout ahead. How should you signal if you need to occupy the left-hand lane?

A. Signal right on approach
B. Give a right signal after entering the roundabout
C. Give no signal on approach
D. Signal left on approach

Answer: A
Description: There are times when, due to the size of your vehicle, you’ll have to take up part of another lane. If you need to do this, make sure that you use effective observation all around. Be aware that other road users might not understand the reasons for your position on the road. You should signal your intentions and take up your position in good time.
Category: The road

Question:
When do drivers of long vehicles need to straddle lanes?

A. When driving on motorways
B. When they need to avoid mounting the kerb
C. When they need to avoid braking sharply
D. When coming to contraflow systems

Answer: B
Description: When you have to straddle the lanes at small roundabouts or junctions, always signal in good time. Be alert for inexperienced road users who may, without realising, put themselves into a dangerous position.
Category: The road

Question:
What should you do as you approach these roadworks?
image: lttk2136.jpg

A. Select a higher gear
B. Use your endurance brake
C. Check your mirrors
D. Flash your headlights

Answer: C
Description: Before changing direction, you should check your mirrors for any vehicles that may be overtaking. An overtaking driver or rider might not have seen the narrowing road ahead. You should let them get past before you move across to the right.
Category: The road

Question:
What should you do when you're overtaking a motorcyclist in very windy conditions?

A. Sound your horn as you pass
B. Keep close as you pass
C. Allow extra room
D. Overtake slowly

Answer: C
Description: Cyclists and motorcyclists may become unbalanced by your vehicle passing too close. Plan ahead and give them plenty of room. Remember that your large vehicle can cause a vacuum, which will suck the rider towards it. The noise and close proximity of your vehicle can also startle them, and could cause them to swerve suddenly.
Category: The road

Question:
You're driving behind two cyclists. They're approaching a roundabout in the left-hand lane. What should you expect them to do?

A. Turn left
B. Go straight ahead
C. Turn right
D. Go in any direction

Answer: D
Description: When following cyclists onto a roundabout, be aware that they might not take the exit you expect them to. Cyclists approaching in the left-hand lane may be turning right. They may not have been able to get into the correct lane due to heavy traffic, so give them room.
Category: The road

Question:
What should you do before you start to overtake a lorry?

A. Look well ahead for uphill gradients
B. Check your position in the left-hand mirror
C. Close right up before pulling out
D. Change quickly to a higher gear

Answer: A
Description: Plan your overtaking carefully. The weight of your vehicle, combined with the restrictions imposed by a speed limiter, is likely to make your vehicle lose speed on uphill gradients. You should take this into consideration before attempting to overtake another moving vehicle.
Category: The road

Question:
You're in the left-hand lane on a three-lane motorway. Why should you check for any vehicles in the right-hand lane before you overtake?

A. They may be moving faster than you
B. They may cut in sharply behind you
C. They may move back to the middle lane as you move out
D. They may accelerate briskly in front of you

Answer: C
Description: Vehicles overtaking in the right-hand lane may return to the centre lane when they've finished their manoeuvre. You should look for this before starting to pull out. Don’t rely on the size of your vehicle to claim right of way.
Category: The road

Question:
What does it indicate if you see white lights on a vehicle at night?

A. It's ahead of you and braking
B. It's moving away from you
C. It's facing towards you
D. It's stationary and facing away from you

Answer: C
Description: At night, you can tell whether a vehicle is facing towards or away from you by the colour of its lights. Additionally, its brake lights or indicators can give you information about its direction and intentions. This information helps you to make safe driving decisions.
Category: The road

Question:
You're driving at night. Why should you ensure that all your lights are clean and working correctly?

A. To prevent the battery from overcharging
B. So that the intensity of street lighting can be reduced
C. So that other road users can see the size of your vehicle
D. To allow following drivers to use dipped headlights

Answer: C
Description: As well as headlights and tail lights, large vehicles have additional lighting to help other road users see the size of the vehicle. All lights should be clean and working properly. Driving at night when your vehicle is poorly lit is dangerous for you and other road users.
Category: The road

Question:
You're driving in fog. When should high-intensity rear fog lights be used?

A. When visibility falls below 400 metres (1312 feet)
B. When visibility falls below 200 metres (656 feet)
C. When visibility falls below 100 metres (328 feet)
D. When visibility falls below 300 metres (984 feet)

Answer: C
Description: In dense fog, large vehicles are no more visible than any other. If visibility falls below 100 metres (328 feet), use your fog lights to help other drivers see you.
Category: The road

Question:
You're driving in fog that's starting to clear. When should you switch off your high-intensity rear fog lights?

A. When visibility is more than 50 metres (164 feet)
B. When visibility is more than 75 metres (246 feet)
C. When visibility is more than 100 metres (328 feet)
D. When visibility is more than 10 metres (32 feet)

Answer: C
Description: Switch off your fog lights when fog starts to clear and visibility improves to more than 100 metres (328 feet). Don’t leave your fog lights on when the fog has cleared, because they can cause unnecessary glare or distraction for other drivers.
Category: The road

Question:
In fast traffic, when should you leave a two-second gap between your vehicle and the one in front?

A. When the roads are icy
B. When you're driving in fog
C. When it's raining and the roads are wet
D. When the roads are dry

Answer: D
Description: In good dry conditions, you should leave a two-second gap between your vehicle and the one ahead. When the weather is bad, you'll have to keep a greater distance, because it will take you longer to stop. In wet weather it will take up to twice the distance; in icy weather this could increase to ten times as far.
Category: The road

Question:
What should you do if you see a vehicle too close behind when you're driving in traffic on the motorway?

A. Briskly accelerate away from the vehicle behind
B. Touch the brake pedal sharply to show your brake lights
C. Switch your rear fog lamps on and off
D. Increase your distance from the vehicle in front

Answer: D
Description: The faster the traffic is moving, the greater the distance that needs to be kept between vehicles to maintain safety margins. If you find another vehicle driving too close behind you, gradually reduce your speed to increase your distance from the vehicle in front. You’ll then be able to brake more gently when you need to, reducing the likelihood of the vehicle behind running into the back of your vehicle.
Category: The road

Question:
What should you do if an overtaking vehicle pulls in too close in front of you?

A. Overtake when you can
B. Slow down
C. Stay close behind
D. Flash your headlights

Answer: B
Description: Always maintain a safe following distance from the vehicle in front. If another vehicle pulls into the gap, slow down to re-establish a safe following distance.
Following too close is dangerous and places you and other road users in unnecessary danger; your view of the road ahead will be seriously reduced, and you won’t be able to see or plan effectively.
Category: The road

Question:
You're driving at 50 mph (80 km/h) on a dry, level road. What gap should you leave between your vehicle and the one in front?

A. At least a one-second gap
B. Two vehicle lengths
C. One vehicle length
D. At least a two-second gap

Answer: D
Description: ‘Tailgating’ – travelling too close to the vehicle in front – is very dangerous, because it doesn't give you enough distance to stop safely.
Leave at least a two-second gap in good conditions, and increase this to four seconds in wet weather.
Category: The road

Question:
You're following a large vehicle. How can you improve your view ahead?

A. Overtake as soon as you can
B. Move over to the left
C. Move over to the right
D. Drop further back

Answer: D
Description: Staying well behind the vehicle in front will improve your view of the road ahead. This will give you more time and room to react to hazards. Use the two-second rule to make sure you’re not too close. Don't move out to the right, as this could put you into the path of an oncoming vehicle or obstruct smaller vehicles that wish to overtake.
Category: The road

Question:
What must you be certain of before you overtake at night?

A. You're outside a built-up area
B. You can see well ahead
C. The road's well lit
D. There's an overtaking lane

Answer: B
Description: It's more difficult to judge speed and distance accurately in the dark. Darkness can also hide bends and dips in the road. Plan ahead, and be sure that you have time and space to complete your overtaking safely.
Category: The road

Question:
How much longer will your stopping distance be in snow than in dry weather?

A. Five times as long
B. Ten times as long
C. Twice as long
D. Four times as long

Answer: B
Description: In icy or snowy weather, your stopping distance can increase by up to ten times. Because snowy weather increases the distance needed to stop, you must look further ahead and leave an increased safety margin.
Category: The road

Question:
How should you slow down or stop when you're driving on an icy road?

A. Use the parking brake in a rapid on-and-off movement
B. Always use the retarder
C. Change down through the gears
D. Brake gently and in good time

Answer: D
Description: When you have to slow down or stop, you should always avoid harsh, late braking. This is particularly important on icy or slippery roads, where you need to brake gently and in good time to make sure you keep control of your vehicle.
Category: The road

Question:
How should you use the brakes in icy weather?

A. After using the gears first
B. Suddenly
C. Gently
D. By pumping the brake pedal

Answer: C
Description: In poor conditions, all braking should be controlled, in good time and when travelling in a straight line. Try to avoid braking and turning at the same time. Look well ahead to assess and plan your actions.
Category: The road

Question:
When should you use the two-second rule?

A. To keep a safe distance from the vehicle in front when it's icy
B. To keep a safe distance from the vehicle in front when conditions are good
C. To keep a safe distance from the vehicle in front in queuing traffic
D. To keep a safe distance from the vehicle in front when it's raining

Answer: B
Description: Use the two-second rule when conditions are good and you're driving on roads carrying faster-moving traffic. Choose a fixed reference point, and when the vehicle ahead passes that point say to yourself 'Only a fool breaks the two-second rule.' If you reach the object before you finish saying this, you’re too close and you need to drop back and check again.
Category: The road

Question:
Why is it dangerous to follow a large goods vehicle too closely?

A. Your field of vision will be seriously reduced
B. Your cab will fill with fumes
C. Your engine will overheat
D. Your brakes will overheat

Answer: A
Description: Staying back will increase your view of the road ahead. This will help you to see any hazards that might occur and will allow you more time to react. It will also allow the driver in front to see you in their mirrors.
Category: The road

Question:
What time gap should you leave when you're following a vehicle on a wet road?

A. At least three seconds
B. At least four seconds
C. At least one second
D. At least two seconds

Answer: B
Description: Wet roads will increase the time it takes you to stop. Four seconds is the minimum gap you should leave on wet roads. This is double the gap you should normally keep from the vehicle in front on good, dry roads.
Category: The road

Question:
The entrances to roundabouts are often slippery when they're wet. How should you deal with this hazard?

A. Stop before emerging
B. Brake in good time
C. Stay in the left-hand lane
D. Use the handbrake

Answer: B
Description: The entrances to roundabouts are often worn. This can make the surface slippery, especially when it's wet. You should plan your approach and brake in good time. 
Category: The road

Question:
You're driving in wet conditions. What should you try to do before braking?

A. Make sure that all spray-suppression equipment is 
working
B. Make sure that there's no mist on your rear-view mirrors
C. Make sure that your vehicle is travelling in a straight line
D. Make sure that the gear lever is in neutral 

Answer: C
Description: If you need to brake when the road surface is wet, do so while your vehicle is travelling in a straight line. This will reduce the risk of skidding. As a professional driver, you should routinely brake in good time, so that you don't brake and change direction at the same time.
Category: The road

Question:

D. You'll need to use a high gear

Answer: A
Description: Always plan well ahead before overtaking. Take into consideration the size of your vehicle and whether there's a gradient ahead. The load on your vehicle will slow you down on an uphill gradient. It may be better to wait until you're on the level before trying to overtake.

A. A motorcycle
B. A taxi
C. A road tanker
D. A sports car

Answer: A
Description: Motorcycles can be very vulnerable to strong side wind. Allow extra room when overtaking them in windy weather. Check your nearside mirror while alongside and before moving back to the left.

Question:

C. At least 73 metres (240 feet)
D. At least 53 metres (175 feet)

Answer: D
Description: You should always leave a safety margin between your vehicle and the one in front. This gap will give you a better view of the road ahead. It will also allow you time to react if the traffic in front changes speed or direction.

Answer: D
Description: When visibility is poor or the road is wet, leave a greater separation distance – at least a four-second time gap from the vehicle in front. You should also reduce speed and use dipped headlights.

Question:
When is trailer swing most likely to occur on a lorry and drawbar combination?

B. While you're steering at slow speed and fully loaded
C. While you're braking on a bend
D. While you're using an endurance brake

Answer: C
Description: The forces that act on your vehicle if you brake while cornering can lead to instability and may cause trailer swing. You should try to plan ahead so that you brake smoothly and in good time as you approach a bend.
Category: Braking systems

Question:
Your vehicle is fitted with a ‘diff-lock’. When would you normally use it?

A. While uncoupling a trailer
B. While driving on muddy construction sites
C. While driving on straight roads
D. While towing an empty trailer

Answer: B
Description: The differential allows the drive wheels to rotate at different speeds; this is necessary for the vehicle to negotiate corners and bends. On a slippery surface, however, it can cause problems: if one wheel has less traction, it can spin, resulting in a complete loss of drive. The 'diff-lock' prevents the wheels from turning independently and so helps to stop this happening.
Category: Braking systems

Question:
What colour is the auxiliary line on a three-line braking system?

A. Red
B. Green
C. Blue
D. Yellow

Answer: C
Description: If you’re driving an articulated vehicle or a trailer combination, it’s vital that you understand the rules that apply to coupling and uncoupling the brake lines. If you take a practical driving test with a trailer, you’ll be expected to demonstrate this during the test. The lines are colour-coded: red is the emergency line, blue is the auxiliary line and yellow is the service line. They must be connected strictly in accordance with the correct procedure.

Question:

A. Red
B. Yellow
C. Black
D. Blue

A. Service
B. Auxiliary

Question:
In frosty weather, what precaution could a lorry driver take to prevent moisture from freezing in the air-brake system?

A. Drain the air tanks daily
B. Cover the air tanks with a blanket
C. Pump the brakes
D. Keep the engine at high revs when starting

Answer: A
Description: You should make sure that you drain the air tanks daily to avoid moisture in the system. Most modern vehicles have an automatic draining system, which should be checked regularly.
Category: Braking systems

Question:
How can a lorry driver avoid brake fade?

A. Make sure that the parking brake is applied before stopping
B. Check that the air pressure is correct
C. Ensure that the air tanks are drained before journeys
D. Select an appropriate gear before downhill gradients

Answer: D
Description: Using the brakes to control a lorry’s speed as it's driven down a hill will cause them to get hot. If they overheat, they can become less effective – a condition known as brake fade. By selecting a low gear, the engine’s resistance will slow the lorry. This reduces the demands on the brakes, making them less likely to overheat.
Category: Braking systems

Question:
When are exhaust brakes most efficient?

A. While travelling at a constant speed on a motorway
B. During stop/start town work
C. At high engine speed, while in low gears
D. At low engine speed, while in high gears

Answer: C
Description: An exhaust brake alters the engine’s exhaust flow, using it to help control the vehicle’s speed. It's most efficient when the engine is running at a high speed and the vehicle is in a low gear, such as when descending a long hill. Using the exhaust brake can relieve the service brakes, preventing them from overheating and fading.
Category: Braking systems

Question:
What's the principal braking system on a lorry called?

A. The service brake
B. The jake brake
C. The parking brake
D. The endurance brake

Answer: A
Description: The service brake is usually operated by the brake pedal. It's used to control the speed of the vehicle and to bring it to a halt safely. It may also incorporate an anti-lock braking system.

Question:
You're driving an articulated lorry. What could happen if you change to a lower gear while you're going too fast?

A. The engine could stall
B. The vehicle could jack-knife
C. The trailer could uncouple
D. The brakes could fail

Answer: B
Description: Severe braking or selecting a gear too low for your road speed can cause the tractor unit to slow more quickly than the trailer. The trailer can then pivot around the coupling (fifth wheel), causing the vehicle to jack-knife. Jack-knifing is more likely to occur with an unladen vehicle, particularly on a bend or curve.
Category: Braking systems

Question:

C. While it's under heavy braking
D. When it's fitted with an endurance brake (retarder)

Answer: C
Description: Heavy braking can cause an articulated vehicle to become unstable and may even lead to jack-knifing; this is more likely to occur when the trailer is unladen.

Question:

B. As soon as the snow has cleared
C. As soon as the vehicle is moving

Answer: C
Description: You must always disengage the diff-lock as soon as the vehicle is moving. The differential allows the rear wheels to revolve at different speeds, and this allows the vehicle to follow a curved path. Attempting to turn with the diff-lock engaged could result in the vehicle continuing straight on.

Question:

B. Apply the footbrake firmly in a pumping action until the vehicle has stopped
C. Apply the handbrake only
D. Apply the footbrake firmly and continuously until the vehicle has stopped

Answer: D
Description: When your vehicle has anti-lock brakes and you need to stop in an emergency, you should keep your foot firmly on the brake pedal until the vehicle stops; this will allow the system to work. Although anti-lock brakes contribute to safety, they don’t reduce your stopping distance or take away the need to drive with good planning and anticipation.

Question:

A. Tyre wear
B. Clutch slip
C. Excessive engine revs
D. Brake fade

Answer: D
Description: Engaging a lower gear and using engine braking will help you to control your speed as you're going downhill. This reduces the demands on the brakes, and helps to prevent them from overheating. This will reduce the likelihood of brake fade.

Question:
You have to drive onto a muddy building site. Why should you switch on your diff-lock?

A. To make the wheels less likely to spin
B. To improve your fuel consumption
C. To increase your engine power
D. To make your steering lighter

Answer: A
Description: Engaging the diff-lock means that the driven wheels are locked together. This reduces the likelihood of wheel spin. Remember to switch off the diff-lock as soon as you're on firm ground again, otherwise you could damage the transmission.
Category: Braking systems

Question:
How will anti-lock brakes improve your vehicle's safety?

A. They let you drive faster on wet roads
B. They allow you to follow other vehicles more closely
C. They help you keep steering control while braking heavily
D. They enable you to brake later than normal

Answer: C
Description: When your steering wheels are locked – as can happen in a skid – you can't steer the vehicle. Anti-lock brakes help you to keep steering control while you're braking heavily, but they aren't a substitute for good forward planning. Anticipation and planning ahead will minimise the risk of skidding more effectively than relying on your braking system.
Category: Braking systems

Question:
What could prevent air pressure from building up in an air-brake system in frosty weather?

A. Moisture drawn in with the air may freeze and cause a blockage
B. The air will contract, reducing the pressure
C. The dampness may cause valves to rust
D. Moisture in the air may form bubbles in the brake fluid

Answer: A
Description: When air is compressed, moisture condenses and collects in the air tanks. This can find its way along the network of pipes connected to the brakes. In frosty weather, the moisture can freeze in the pipes, blocking them completely. On modern vehicles, the air is dried before it's compressed and the air tanks drain automatically to shed any moisture. On older vehicles, the air tanks need draining manually.
Category: Braking systems

Question:
What should you do if the brake air-pressure warning light comes on while you're driving?

A. Stop and get help without delay
B. Build up the pressure by accelerating
C. Report the fault when you return to your depot
D. Drain the air tanks and continue normally

Answer: A
Description: When a warning light or device indicating a loss of brake pressure comes on, you must stop safely and get the fault put right immediately. The safety of you, your load, your passengers and all other road users is at risk.
Category: Braking systems

Question:
