A. Keep the parking brake on
B. Report it as a fault 
C. Switch your engine off
D. Engage the clutch

Answer: A
Description: Even though the warning light is showing, there may be sufficient pressure to release the parking brake. However, you mustn't do this, because there may not be enough air pressure to operate the service brake. 
Category: Braking systems

Question:
Your vehicle is fitted with an anti-lock braking system. What's it designed to allow you to do?

A. Stop safely in an emergency
B. Drive at faster speeds
C. Apply the brakes more quickly
D. Brake much later than normal

Answer: A
Description: Anti-lock braking systems sense when the wheels are about to lock. The sensor control releases the brakes and immediately applies them again. It will do this many times per second. This both prevents skidding and enables the driver to steer – something that's impossible when the steering wheels are skidding.
Category: Braking systems

C. Before every journey
D. Before each service

Answer: C
Description: Modern anti-lock braking systems rely on electronics for their operation. A warning light on the dashboard shows that the system is operating. This light will usually go out when the vehicle reaches about 6 mph (10 km/h).

Question:

D. Apply minimum force to the brake pedal

Category: Braking systems

Question:
What's ‘brake fade’?

A. Reduction of air pressure
B. Low hydraulic brake fluid level
C. Smooth progressive braking
D. Reduction of braking effectiveness

Answer: D
Description: Continually using the brakes could cause them to overheat. When that happens, they become less effective. This is called brake fade, and it occurs most often when the driver has to control the vehicle's speed on a long downhill gradient. To help prevent brake fade, use the endurance brake (retarder) and a lower gear to keep the vehicle's speed in check, rather than the wheel-mounted brakes.
Category: Braking systems

Question:
‘Brake fade’ is a loss of effectiveness of the brakes when they overheat. When would 'brake fade' be most likely to happen?

A. On a long downhill gradient
B. On the approach to hazards
C. On a long uphill gradient
D. On a long journey

Answer: A
Description: Continuous use of the brakes will cause them to overheat, and in extreme cases they’ll become ineffective. When you’re going downhill, the momentum of your vehicle will cause you to gather speed very quickly. Use the endurance brake (retarder) and stay in a low gear to reduce the need to use the brakes.
Category: Braking systems

B. When you stop or park

Question:
Your vehicle is fully loaded. Where should you be braking when dealing with bends?

A. When driving in a straight line
B. As you start to turn the wheel
C. When halfway around the bend
D. As close to the bend as possible

Answer: A
Description: When a vehicle changes direction, forces are applied to the vehicle and its load. Braking at the same time can result in additional forces being introduced, and this can lead to a loss of control. For this reason, braking should be carried out while driving in a straight line, so preventing these forces from acting together.

Question:

B. The brake pedal has little resistance
C. The brake pedal feels spongy when pressed
D. The brake pedal travels a long way

Answer: A
Description: The pump creates a vacuum in the servo unit. This reduces the amount of pressure you need to apply to the brake pedal. Without this vacuum, it's extremely difficult to press the brake pedal down.

Question:
Which component will last longer when you use a retarder?

A. The catalytic converter
B. The brake linings
C. The exhaust system
D. The transmission

Answer: B
Description: By using a retarder, the life of the brake linings is extended. This is because a retarder works by slowing the vehicle without using the wheel-mounted brakes.
Category: Braking systems

Question:
What should you do when an air-pressure warning device activates?

A. Stop and have the fault put right
B. Pump the brake pedal repeatedly
C. Drain the air tanks
D. Continue to drive the vehicle

Answer: A
Description: Air-brake systems are fitted with a warning device that operates if the air pressure in the tanks drops below a safe level. There may be a warning buzzer and/or pressure gauges. You must be aware of the function of all gauges on your vehicle, and check them as you drive.
Category: Braking systems

Question:
You're driving down a snow-covered hill. Why should you take care when using an independent endurance brake (retarder)?

A. Your speed could increase
B. Your brakes could overheat
C. Compressed air could escape
D. The drive wheels could lock

Answer: D
Description: Select an appropriate gear in good time and, if your vehicle has a dashboard-mounted lever, apply the endurance brake (retarder) in stages. Braking too much, too soon may result in locking your drive wheels.
Category: Braking systems

Question:
What should you avoid when using an independent endurance brake (retarder) on slippery roads?

A. The front wheels spinning
B. Brake-pad wear
C. The drive wheels locking
D. Anti-skid road surfaces

Answer: C
Description: The endurance brake (retarder) usually operates by applying resistance, via the transmission, to the vehicle’s driven wheels. If the road is slippery, the tyres may lose grip and the wheels will lock.
Category: Braking systems

Question:
You're about to drive an unfamiliar vehicle. What should you do if you think there may be moisture in the air-brake reservoir?

A. Find out whether you need to drain the system manually
B. Leave the engine running for a while before driving
C. Nothing; it's the vehicle owner’s responsibility
D. Assume the system has automatic drain valves

Answer: A
Description: Moisture in the braking system can cause serious problems, especially in cold weather, when it could freeze and stop the brakes from working. Most modern vehicles have a system that drains automatically, but make sure you know which system is fitted to any vehicle that you drive. 
Category: Braking systems

Question:
You've been asked to drive a fully loaded petrol tanker back to the depot. It has a maximum authorised mass of 10 tonnes. What must you have before you can drive this vehicle?

A. A request from the police to move a dangerous load
B. A valid ADR driver training certificate
C. A fully qualified tanker driver with you for the journey
D. A copy of the vehicle's insurance certificate

Answer: B
Description: Drivers of vehicles carrying dangerous goods are required to hold an ADR driver training certificate. This certificate is valid for five years and is issued by DVLA when you've attended an approved course and successfully completed the examination.
Category: Essential documents

Question:
Who's responsible for making sure that cargo arrives undamaged?

A. The loader
B. The sender
C. The driver
D. The packer

Answer: C
Description: The driver mustn't allow any cargo to be damaged during transit, loading or unloading. This requires a responsible attitude to safeguard the load at all times.
Category: Essential documents

Question:
How many copies of the CMR consignment note are required?

A. Five
B. Three
C. Two
D. Four

Answer: D
Description: The full name of the CMR is the 'Convention on the Contract for the International Carriage of Goods by Road'. You'll need this document to transport goods internationally by road. Of the four copies required, the consignor, consignee and originator all have one copy, and the fourth travels with the vehicle.
Category: Essential documents

Question:
You hold a full category C licence. What does this entitle you to tow?

A. A trailer with more than one axle
B. A trailer up to 750 kg
C. A trailer of any weight
D. A curtain-sided trailer

Answer: B
Description: When you pass a test to obtain a C or C1 licence, you can tow trailers up to 750 kg. You can do this without taking a further test.
Category: Essential documents

Question:
You're delivering boxes of chilled food to a supermarket. What specific training would you need?

A. Hygiene procedures
B. Waste-handling procedures
C. Ecosafe driving procedures
D. ADR procedures

Answer: A
Description: Chilled foods are transported at temperatures above freezing point. Drivers need to be trained in hygiene procedures and how to operate refrigeration units.

You'll be driving your vehicle in Europe. Which of these documents must you carry?

A. The vehicle service record
B. Your medical examination form
C. Your national driving licence 
D. The vehicle workshop manual

Answer: C
Description: As well as your driving licence, you'll need to carry the insurance certificate and vehicle registration document. Other documentation may also be needed for some countries. Check this before starting your journey.

Question:
What condition could prevent you from holding a lorry or bus licence?

A. Dermatitis
B. Stomach upset
C. Dyslexia
D. Partial blindness

Answer: D
Description: Any medical condition that could affect your ability to drive a lorry or a bus safely may prevent you from holding a licence. These conditions include serious visual impairment, heart disease and some mental disorders. For more information about medical standards, you should contact the Drivers Medical Branch, DVLA, Swansea.
Category: Essential documents

Question:
You've been convicted of a drink-drive offence and banned from driving. Which entitlement will this ban affect?

A. Your bus entitlement
B. Your car entitlement
C. Your lorry entitlement
D. Your entitlement to drive all motor vehicles

Answer: D
Description: The dangers of drink-driving are well publicised. Anyone convicted of this offence will lose their entitlement to drive any motor vehicle on the road.
Category: Essential documents

Question:
You're found to be two-and-a-half times over the legal drink-drive limit and are disqualified from driving. Before regaining your licence, who will you have to satisfy that you don't have an alcohol problem?

A. The local hospital
B. The Driver and Vehicle Standards Agency
C. The Driver and Vehicle Licensing Agency
D. Alcoholics Anonymous

Answer: C
Description: If you're disqualified from driving because you were two-and-a-half times over the legal limit, you'll be classified as a high-risk offender. Before you can regain your licence, you'll have to satisfy the Driver and Vehicle Licensing Agency (DVLA) that you don't have an alcohol problem.
Category: Essential documents

Question:
For how long is a Statutory Off-Road Notification (SORN) valid?

A. Until the vehicle is insured and MOT’d
B. Until the vehicle is used on the road
C. Until the vehicle is taxed, sold or scrapped
D. Until the vehicle is repaired or modified

Answer: C
Description: A SORN allows you to keep a vehicle off the road and untaxed. The SORN remains valid until the vehicle is taxed, sold or scrapped. If you buy a vehicle that has a SORN, the SORN will finish as soon as you buy it. You'll need to make a new SORN if you want to keep the vehicle off the road and untaxed.
Category: Essential documents

Question:
What's a Statutory Off-Road Notification (SORN)?

A. Information held by insurance companies to check the vehicle is insured
B. A notification to tell DVLA that a vehicle isn't being used on the road
C. A notification to tell DVSA that a vehicle doesn't have a current MOT
D. Information kept by the police about the owner of the vehicle

Answer: B
Description: If you want to keep a vehicle untaxed and off the public road, you must make a SORN. It's an offence not to do so. When you've made a SORN, you won’t have to pay vehicle tax, but you also won't be able to use the vehicle on the road. The SORN remains valid until your vehicle is taxed, sold, scrapped or exported.
Category: Essential documents

Question:
What's the maximum fine for driving without insurance?

A. £5000
B. £1000
C. Unlimited
D. £500

Answer: C
Description: It’s a serious offence to drive without insurance. As well as an unlimited fine, you may be disqualified or given penalty points. 
Category: Essential documents

Question:
What's the current fine for each person illegally carried into the UK?

A. Up to £3000
B. Up to £1000
C. Up to £4000
D. Up to £2000

Answer: D
Description: The importation of illegal immigrants into the UK carries heavy penalties. A fine of up to £2000 can be imposed for each illegal immigrant. This fine can be imposed on each ‘responsible person’, which includes the vehicle owner, hirer and driver.
Category: Essential documents

Question:
Drivers can be fined for bringing illegal immigrants into the UK. Who else can be fined?

A. The vehicle hirer
B. The vehicle insurer
C. The vehicle manufacturer
D. The vehicle repairer

Answer: A
Description: There are heavy fines for those convicted of bringing illegal immigrants into the UK. This can mean a fine for each illegal person carried. The fine can be imposed on each ‘responsible person’, including the vehicle driver, owner and hirer.
Category: Essential documents

Question:
How can vehicle operators help to prevent the carriage of illegal immigrants?

A. By having effective mobile communications 
B. By taking out liability insurance
C. By using vehicle tracking devices
D. By using an effective vehicle security system

Answer: D
Description: Current legislation requires all operators to set up an ‘effective system’ to help prevent the carriage of illegal immigrants. This should include vehicle security and checking using a checklist. Failure to do this will incur penalties.
Category: Essential documents

Question:
You're returning to the UK and are about to board a ferry. An immigration officer asks to see your documentation. What must you show them immediately?

A. Your driver’s hours record
B. Your vehicle registration document
C. Your driving licence
D. Your operator documentation

Answer: D
Description: Operators must set up an ‘effective system’ to prevent the carriage of illegal immigrants. This should include documentation with advice on vehicle security and a list of checks to be made. These papers should be produced immediately if an immigration officer asks to see them.
Category: Essential documents

Question:
A driver is convicted of bringing illegal immigrants into the UK. How is the fine calculated?

A. For each court attendance they make
B. For each journey they made in the last year
C. For each person they bring in
D. For each family group they bring in

Answer: C
Description: If convicted, the current fine for each illegal immigrant brought into the UK is £2000. This fine can be imposed on each responsible person; this includes the vehicle driver, owner and hirer.
Category: Essential documents

Question:
The Driver Certificate of Professional Competence (Driver CPC) requires you to take training every five years. How many hours of training must you take?

A. 35 hours
B. 40 hours
C. 30 hours
D. 45 hours

Answer: A
Description: To keep your Driver CPC, you need to take 35 hours of training every five years. This can be split into sessions of at least seven hours each, so you can take one training day a year over the five years if that suits you. The penalties for non-compliance are the same as those for driving without a licence.
Category: Essential documents

Question:
You'll need to take 35 hours of training to maintain your Driver Certificate of Professional Competence (Driver CPC). Over what period must this be carried out?

A. Three years
B. One year
C. Ten years
D. Five years

Answer: D
Description: You must take 35 hours of training every five years to maintain your Driver CPC. This can be done at any time during the five years: all at once or split into sessions of at least seven hours each. The penalties for non-compliance are the same as those for driving without a licence.
Category: Essential documents

Question:
Every five years, you must complete further training to keep your Driver Certificate of Professional Competence (Driver CPC). How many hours of training must you complete over those five years?

A. 35 hours
B. 40 hours
C. 30 hours
D. 25 hours

Answer: A
Description: Drivers are required to take 35 hours of training every five years to maintain their Driver CPC. This can be split into shorter sessions of at least seven hours each. These can be spread over the five years, so effectively one day’s training is taken each year. The penalties for non-compliance are the same as those for driving without a licence.
Category: Essential documents

Question:

A. A hygiene test
B. An eyesight test
C. A numeracy test
D. A literacy test

Answer: B
Description: If you apply for a PCV or LGV licence, you must demonstrate that your eyesight is good enough to drive safely. DVLA (or DVA in Northern Ireland) can give you specific information about this. It's your responsibility to tell DVLA or DVA if your eyesight changes or you can’t meet the requirements.

Question:
Your vehicle leaks diesel fuel on a roundabout. Who will this affect most?

A. Towed vehicles
B. Drivers of three-wheeled vehicles
C. Motorcyclists
D. Car drivers

Answer: C
Description: When diesel fuel spills onto the road, it makes the road surface extremely slippery. This can cause danger for all types of vehicle, but particularly for those with two wheels, which rely on their tyres' grip to remain upright.

B. Motorcycles

Description: You should be aware that motorcyclists are likely to be affected by side wind and can be blown into your path. Adjust your speed so that you can stop or take avoiding action safely if necessary.

Description: Learners might take longer to react to traffic situations. Don’t unnerve and intimidate them by driving up close behind.

Question:

image: lttk2140.jpg

A. Driving slowly
B. Keeping well back
C. Sounding your horn
D. Giving arm signals

Answer: C
Description: When passing horses, allow plenty of space, slow down and stop if you need to. Animals are easily frightened by sudden or loud noises and can quickly become uncontrollable, so don’t sound your horn or rev the engine.

Question:

A. Drive in front of them
B. Drive behind them
C. Sound your horn at them
D. Give way to them

Answer: D
Description: At a pelican crossing, the green light means you may go, but you must give way to anyone still crossing. If someone hasn’t finished crossing, be patient. People with mobility difficulties can struggle to cross in the time allowed by the lights. 
Category: Other road users

D. Give way to the pedestrians who are already crossing

Answer: D
Description: Always look into the road you’re entering. If pedestrians are already crossing, be considerate and give way to them. Don't wave or signal them to hurry; they have priority here.

Question:

B. Turn right
C. Go ahead
D. Go in any direction

Answer: D
Description: Horses and their riders will move more slowly than other road users. They might not have time to cut across heavy traffic to take up a position in the offside lane when they're turning right; it could also be hazardous for them to do so. Therefore, a horse and rider may approach a roundabout in the left-hand lane, even though they’re turning right.

Question:

B. To make sure the side road is clear
C. To look for pedestrians about to cross
D. To check for emerging traffic

Answer: A
Description: Always check your right-hand mirror and blind spot just before you make a right turn, as another vehicle could be overtaking you. Motorcyclists often filter along the outside of traffic queues. Keep checking all your mirrors while you're waiting to turn, because situations behind you can change quickly. 
Category: Other road users

Question:
You're driving past a line of parked cars. What should you do if you notice a ball bouncing out into the road ahead?
image: lttk2150.jpg

A. Continue driving at the same speed and sound your horn
B. Stop and wave the children across to fetch their ball
C. Continue driving at the same speed and flash your headlights
D. Slow down and be prepared to stop for children

Answer: D
Description: Beware of children playing in the street and running out into the road. If a ball bounces out from the pavement, slow down and stop if necessary. Don’t encourage anyone to fetch the ball from the road. Other road users might not see your signal and you might lead a child into danger.
Category: Other road users

Question:
What should you do just before turning right from a main road into a side road?

A. Cancel your right-turn signal
B. Select first gear
C. Stop and set the handbrake
D. Check for traffic passing on your right

Answer: D
Description: Motorcyclists can often pass slow or stationary traffic because of the relatively small size of their vehicle. Take a last look in your right-hand mirror to check for motorcyclists and so avoid turning across their path.
Category: Other road users

Question:
You're driving past a bus that's waiting at a bus stop on the other side of the road. Why should you be careful?

A. The bus may move off suddenly
B. The bus may remain stationary
C. Pedestrians may come from behind the bus
D. The bus may have broken down

Answer: C
Description: Watch out for pedestrians if you see a bus ahead. They may not be able to see you if they’re crossing behind the bus.
Category: Other road users

Question:
How should you overtake horse riders?

A. Drive slowly and leave plenty of room
B. Drive up close and overtake as soon as possible
C. Speed isn't important but allow plenty of room
D. Use your horn just once to warn them

Answer: A
Description: Horses are easily frightened, so pass them slowly and carefully, giving them as much room as possible. On country roads, expect farm animals, horses, pedestrians and farm vehicles. Always be prepared to slow down or stop.
Category: Other road users

Question:
Where in particular should you look out for motorcyclists?

A. At a road junction
B. Near a service area
C. When entering a car park
D. At a filling station

Answer: A
Description: Motorcyclists and cyclists are smaller and usually more difficult to see than other vehicles. Look out for them at junctions; failing to see them can lead to a collision.

Question:
While driving at night, you see a pedestrian ahead. What does it mean if they're wearing reflective clothing and carrying a red light?

A. You're approaching an organised walk
B. You're approaching men at work
C. You're approaching slow-moving vehicles
D. You're approaching an incident blackspot

Answer: A
Description: Pedestrians who are part of an organised walk using the road at night should wear bright or reflective clothing. The walker in front should display a white light, while the one at the back should display a red light. Be particularly careful, slow down and give the walkers plenty of room.
Category: Other road users

Question:
Which road users are more vulnerable at night in built-up areas?

A. Ambulance drivers
B. Drivers of black taxi cabs
C. Drivers of double-deck vehicles
D. Cyclists

Answer: D
Description: Look out for cyclists who don't have lights on. Also be aware that pedestrians – especially those in dark clothing – may be difficult to see.

Question:
You're about to overtake a motorcyclist when they look around over their right shoulder. What's the most likely reason for them doing this?

A. Something has fallen from the machine
B. The rider intends to move to the right
C. The rear tyre is flat
D. The drive chain is slack

Answer: B
Description: Understanding other road users' behaviour can help you anticipate their next action. On this occasion it could prevent a serious incident. This type of assessment is part of the forward planning of a professional driver.
Category: Other road users

Question:
Why should you allow extra room for motorcyclists when they're riding through roadworks?

A. They may swerve to avoid potholes
B. The traffic may be in single file
C. There may be temporary traffic lights
D. There may be a reduced speed limit

Answer: A
Description: Motorcyclists can ride through narrow gaps in traffic and generally don’t take up as much room as a car. However, other factors, including the road surface, can affect their stability. Give them an extra safety margin whenever possible.
Category: Other road users

Question:
You're following a motorcyclist along a potholed road. How should you adjust your driving to take account of this situation?

A. Stay close behind them
B. Drive alongside them
C. Give them extra room
D. Try to pass them

Answer: C
Description: Good forward planning can help you keep other road users out of trouble. Information to help you do this is available if you look for it. Watch for clues: for example, a motorcyclist taking a ‘lifesaver’ look over their shoulder could be about to change direction.
Category: Other road users

Question:
Which vehicles are most at risk from spilt diesel fuel?

A. Empty tankers
B. Towed vehicles
C. Motorcycles
D. Fire engines

Answer: C
Description: Where the road surface has been made slippery (for example, by spilt diesel fuel), motorcyclists are particularly vulnerable to skidding.
Category: Other road users

Question:
You're driving in a town. What should you do when you see this sign on a stationary bus ahead?
image: lttk2143.jpg

A. Wait until it moves off
B. Expect the driver will be looking after the children
C. Accelerate quickly
D. Drive past slowly

Answer: D
Description: Children getting off the bus will be hidden from your view, and they may not be able to see you. Even if they can see you, they may have poor judgement of danger. You should drive slowly as you pass the bus and be ready to stop.
Category: Other road users

Question:
What should you do when you're following a scooter on a poor road surface?
image: lttk2151.jpg

A. Stay close behind until you can pass
B. Overtake without any delay
C. Stay well back and allow them room
D. Sound your horn as you get close

Answer: C
Description: On a poor road surface, the rider may need to move out to avoid potholes. You may not get much warning. A look to the right or a ‘lifesaver’ check may warn you that they're about to move out. Stay well back and allow the rider plenty of room until you can pass safely. 
Category: Other road users

Question:
At toucan crossings, pedestrians share the crossing with which other road users?

A. Cyclists
B. Horse riders
C. Trams
D. Motorcyclists

Answer: A
Description: A toucan crossing is signal-controlled, but unlike a pelican crossing it doesn't have a flashing amber light in the sequence. Cyclists and pedestrians cross together, and cyclists are allowed to ride their bicycles over the crossing.
Category: Other road users

Question:
You're driving on a dual carriageway. What type of vehicle must use a flashing amber beacon on this road?

A. A mobility scooter
B. A fire engine 
C. An ambulance
D. A doctor’s car on call

Answer: A
Description: Small battery-powered vehicles are often used by disabled people. On unrestricted dual carriageways, these vehicles must show a flashing amber light. Be very careful, as they have a maximum speed of 8 mph. You may see other slow-moving vehicles with amber flashing lights, such as agricultural vehicles. 
Category: Other road users

Question:
You're driving near a school in heavy traffic. What should you do when there are children walking close to the kerb on your side of the road?

A. Wave at them to move back from the kerb
B. Stop for a moment to see what they do
C. Move to the other side of the road
D. Drive slowly until you're clear of the area

Answer: D
Description: Children can be unpredictable, and when they're in groups they may fool around and push each other into the road. You should drive with extreme caution when you're near them. You need to be ready to stop suddenly.
Category: Other road users

Question:
You're driving on a road with an uneven surface. What should you do if you're following a motorcyclist along this road?

A. Allow extra room in case the rider swerves to avoid potholes
B. Drive close behind and get ready to overtake
C. Drive closely to shield the rider
D. Leave less room so the rider can see you in their mirrors

Answer: A
Description: Never follow any road user too closely. This is particularly important when you're following scooter or motorcycle riders, or cyclists. They might brake or swerve suddenly; for example, to avoid a pothole on a road with a poor surface.
Category: Other road users

Question:
You wish to turn left into a side road. What should you do if there's a cyclist in front as you approach the junction?

A. Overtake the cyclist before the junction
B. Sound your horn to warn the cyclist to wait
C. Wait until the cyclist has passed the junction
D. Drive alongside and watch the cyclist in your mirrors

Answer: C
Description: Stay back and allow the cyclist to proceed. You mustn't cut across in front of them. Also be aware of any cyclists who may try to pass on your left as you slow for the turn.

Question:
You're waiting to turn left at a junction. In your mirror you can see a cyclist moving up between the kerb and the nearside of your vehicle. How should you deal with the cyclist?

A. Steer to the left to make them dismount
B. Move off and make them wait for you
C. Tell them to move out of your way
D. Allow them to move in front of you

Answer: D
Description: Always be aware of your limited vision around your vehicle, due to its size and shape. Never move off without checking along the nearside of your vehicle. You should be aware of the possibility of cyclists and motorcyclists getting trapped between your vehicle and the kerb.
Category: Other road users

Question:
You're approaching a roundabout. You see a cyclist signal right. Why do they keep to the left?

A. It's a safer route for a cyclist
B. They're going to turn left
C. The Highway Code doesn't apply to cyclists
D. It's a quicker route for a cyclist

Answer: A
Description: The cyclist may not be able to get into a right-hand lane due to heavy traffic. Give them room, as they may not be taking the exit you expect.

Question:
You're entering a roundabout. What should you do if a cyclist in front of you is signalling to turn right?

A. Sound the horn
B. Overtake on the right
C. Allow plenty of room
D. Overtake on the left

Answer: C
Description: Allow the cyclist plenty of room. Give them space and be prepared for them to change direction. To stay safe, they may travel around the roundabout in the left-hand lane.
Category: Other road users

Question:
A group of horse riders comes towards you. What should you do if the leading rider’s horse becomes nervous of your presence?

A. Increase speed to pass the riders quickly
B. Brake gently to a stop until they've passed
C. Continue driving, keeping well to the left
D. Brake quickly to a stop, applying the parking brake

Answer: B
Description: If any animal you pass on the road becomes unsettled, you should brake gently and come to a stop. A nervous animal is unpredictable, so you should wait until it has settled or passed by. Other road users behind you may have a limited view of the hazard, so use your mirrors and give clear signals if necessary.
Category: Other road users

Question:

B. Tractor
C. Bicycle
D. Milk float

Answer: C
Description: Always check carefully for cyclists when emerging from a junction. Bicycles, being much narrower than any other vehicle, can be quite difficult to see.

Question:
Why are motorcyclists more at risk from other road users?

A. They often break down
B. They're easy to see
C. They can't give arm signals
D. They're easily overlooked

Answer: D
Description: Always look for the more vulnerable road users, such as motorcyclists, cyclists, pedestrians (especially children), animals and horse riders. All need your consideration. Motorcycles are relatively small, but they can move just as fast as other vehicles, making them easy to overlook.
Category: Other road users

Question:
Which of these is the main cause of collisions involving motorcycles?

A. Other drivers
B. Other motorcyclists
C. Wet roads
D. Icy roads

Answer: A
Description: The main reason why there are so many collisions at junctions is that drivers fail to see motorcyclists. A bright jacket or single headlight may help you identify an approaching motorcyclist, but you should be aware that not all motorcyclists wear bright clothing or use their headlights during the day.
Category: Other road users

A. Private-hire taxis
B. Filtering motorcyclists
C. Breakdown vehicles
D. Traffic cones

Answer: B
Description: In slow-moving traffic, particularly on dual carriageways or motorways, always be on the lookout for motorcyclists who approach from behind and filter through narrow gaps between vehicles.

Question:
Which road users are especially at risk at a road junction?

A. Lorry drivers
B. Car drivers
C. Bus drivers
D. Motorcyclists

Answer: D
Description: Junctions are especially risky for some road users – particularly motorcyclists, cyclists, pedestrians and mobility-scooter users. Their small size means they're easily hidden from view. At busy junctions, scan the near, middle and far distance to identify all hazards before emerging with a long vehicle.
Category: Other road users

A. Near zebra crossings

Question:
You're driving towards a zebra crossing. What should you do if you see that a person in a wheelchair is waiting to cross? 

A. Continue on your way
B. Be prepared to stop
C. Wave to the person to wait
D. Wave to the person to cross

Answer: B
Description: Prepare to slow down and stop, as you would for a person without a disability. Don’t wave them across, as other traffic may not stop.

Question:
How will a school crossing patrol signal you to stop?

A. By displaying a ‘stop’ sign
B. By pointing to children on the opposite pavement
C. By displaying a red light
D. By giving you an arm signal

Answer: A
Description: If a school crossing patrol steps out into the road with a 'stop' sign, you must stop. Don’t wave anyone across the road or get impatient and rev your engine.

Question:
There's a slow-moving motorcyclist ahead of you. What should you do if you're unsure what the rider is going to do?

A. Pass on the left
B. Stay behind
C. Move closer
D. Pass on the right

Answer: B
Description: The motorcyclist might be turning right, changing direction or unsure of their destination. Stay behind until the rider has made a move or you're sure you can pass safely. Don't intimidate them by moving too close.

Question:
Which road users are more vulnerable at road junctions?

A. Lorry drivers
B. Taxi drivers
C. Cyclists
D. Car drivers

Answer: C
Description: Road junctions can be especially dangerous for some road users, especially those that are small and more easily overlooked. Effective observation is necessary to ensure you don't overlook anything.

Question:
You're driving on a single carriageway road. What should you do when you see horse riders ahead?
image: lttk2140.jpg

A. Switch on your vehicle's hazard warning lights
B. Check your mirrors and prepare to slow down
C. Move into the middle of the road
D. Signal right to show you're going to pass them

Answer: B
Description: Look well ahead and be ready to deal with any hazards you see coming up, such as animals in the road. Horses are easily scared by the noise of an engine and the size of your vehicle may also be intimidating. Approach them as slowly and quietly as you can. 
Category: Other road users

Question:
As you approach a pelican crossing, the lights change to green. What should you do if an elderly couple are halfway across?

A. Flash your lights in case they haven't heard you
B. Wait patiently and give them time to finish crossing
C. Wave at them to cross as quickly as they can
D. Rev your engine to make them hurry

Answer: B
Description: When the lights turn to green, you may drive on, but only if the crossing is clear. You should wait for any pedestrians to finish crossing, regardless of their age. Allow them to cross the road at their own pace; don't try to hurry them in any way.
Category: Other road users

Question:
What should you do when you're following a motorcyclist on an uneven road?

A. Allow less room, so you can be seen in their mirrors
B. Allow the same room as you would any other road user
C. Allow extra room, in case they swerve to avoid potholes
D. Overtake them immediately

Answer: C
Description: Potholes and raised drain covers in the road can unsteady a motorcyclist. They may suddenly swerve to avoid these uneven surfaces. Watch out at places where the road is in poor condition and this is likely to occur.
Category: Other road users

Question:
Why do you have to be alert for motorcyclists in queues of traffic?

A. They may have panniers fitted to their motorcycle
B. They may ride with their headlights on dipped beam
C. They may ride in single file
D. They may be filtering between the lanes

Answer: D
Description: In queuing traffic, motorcyclists may take the opportunity to filter between the lanes. Be aware that they may pass on either side and very close. Stay alert and always check your mirrors and blind spots before moving off, changing lanes or turning.
Category: Other road users

Question:
You're driving past parked cars. What should you do if you notice a bicycle wheel sticking out between them?

A. Slow down and be prepared to stop for a cyclist
B. Brake sharply and flash your headlights
C. Slow down and wave the cyclist across
D. Accelerate past quickly and sound your horn

Answer: A
Description: Scan the road as you drive. Try to anticipate hazards by being aware of the places where they're likely to occur; for example, pedestrians and cyclists emerging between parked cars on a busy street. If you're prepared, you'll be able to slow down or stop in good time.
Category: Other road users

Question:
What do yellow zigzag lines on the road outside a school mean?
image: lttk2147.jpg

A. You mustn't wait or park on these lines
B. Sound your horn to alert other road users
C. You mustn't drive over these lines
D. Stop to allow children to cross

Answer: A
Description: Parking on the yellow zigzag lines will block the view of the school entrance. This will endanger the lives of children wanting to cross the road on their way to and from school.
Category: Other road users

Question:
You're driving on a main road. What should you do just before turning right into a side road?

A. Check for traffic overtaking on your right
B. Flash your headlights
C. Steer over to the left
D. Adjust your interior mirror

Answer: A
Description: Just before turning, a check in the offside mirror will help you to see any cyclist or motorcyclist passing on your offside. This check may help to prevent a serious incident from developing.
Category: Other road users

Question:
Where should you take particular care to look for motorcyclists and cyclists?

A. At junctions
B. In one-way streets
C. At zebra crossings
D. On dual carriageways

Answer: A
Description: Motorcyclists and cyclists may be more difficult to see, especially at junctions. They can be easily hidden by obstructions such as other vehicles, and the small size of an approaching motorcycle may make it difficult to judge its speed and distance. It's vital that you don't emerge until you're sure it's safe.
Category: Other road users
